  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        scope : 'name email',

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5707171372811952525">„Miecz przeznaczenia” jest zbiorem opowiadań stanowiących swoistą kontynuację przygód Geralta ze zbioru „Ostatnie życzenie”, a zarazem poprzedza historię opisaną w „Sadze o wiedźminie”. Generalnie opowiadania składające się na omawiany zbiór nie różnią się niczym od napisanych wcześniej. Geralt dzięki swojej sile, odwadze i inteligencji walczy z potworami bądź w inny sposó</span>
  <span id="freeText5707171372811952525" style="display:none">„Miecz przeznaczenia” jest zbiorem opowiadań stanowiących swoistą kontynuację przygód Geralta ze zbioru „Ostatnie życzenie”, a zarazem poprzedza historię opisaną w „Sadze o wiedźminie”. Generalnie opowiadania składające się na omawiany zbiór nie różnią się niczym od napisanych wcześniej. Geralt dzięki swojej sile, odwadze i inteligencji walczy z potworami bądź w inny sposób stara się pomagać ludziom. Świat, w którym rozgrywa się akcja, jest przedstawiony w sposób niezwykle plastyczny, co sprawia, iż można go sobie bez większych problemów wyobrazić. Książka przesiąknięta jest emocjami, marzeniami i wartościami. Na kartach opowiadań widzimy miłość, poświęcenie, honor, determinację spowodowaną zamiarem udzielenia pomocy ukochanemu, przywiązanie do własnej ziemi.</span>

          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

<div id="review_2564988793" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2564988793" />
    <a title="James Tivendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale"><img alt="James Tivendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605206526p2/10282461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2564988793?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Tivendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Tivendale" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale">James Tivendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473211537" href="/book/show/18215192-sword-of-destiny">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2564988793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1992116534571097847">Much like The Last Wish before, Sword of Destiny is a collection of short stories following a talented witcher called Geralt of Rivia. Although you can start the series with Blood of Elves which is where the full-length novels commence, I can't recommend enough that even though a handful of these short stories are hit-and-miss, that they will add considerable depth to the future narrative arcs.<br/><br/>The Last Wish featured mostly isolated stories with the Witcher tackling a certain monstrosity for a se</span>
  <span id="freeText1992116534571097847" style="display:none">Much like The Last Wish before, Sword of Destiny is a collection of short stories following a talented witcher called Geralt of Rivia. Although you can start the series with Blood of Elves which is where the full-length novels commence, I can't recommend enough that even though a handful of these short stories are hit-and-miss, that they will add considerable depth to the future narrative arcs.<br /><br />The Last Wish featured mostly isolated stories with the Witcher tackling a certain monstrosity for a set payment. He travels around the world to where his peculiar killing and magic techniques are needed to tackle a problem and individuals will hire him. In the first book, apart from a couple of brief interludes, there were no recurring characters. It was solely about a certain adventure at one end of the world and then another a thousand miles away. Sword of Destiny features a handful of main characters from the series who become more fleshed out as there presence recurs. Geralt's friend and lady loving bard Dandelion, his mysterious sorceress love interest Yennefer and a potential child of destiny called Ciri. If you've played The Witcher computer games I imagine you a familiar with these characters, the sort of missions set and the monsters the Witcher is assigned to eradicate, and how beautiful and vast this created world is. <br /><br />I found the stories in The Last Wish more consistent but two or three of my favourites are from this entry. If you decide to read the short story collections first I'd truly recommend starting with The Last Wish and not Sword of Destiny. Two stories in The Witcher #1, one including Yennefer and one including a Queen and a Princess, add huge depth to the action and events that occur in this collection, especially with certain relationship complexities.<br /><br />The Witcher tales are exciting and addictive to say that a story can be finished in about half an hour. Sapkowski doesn't dumb down the world and there are a plethora of complex characters and demons throughout these pages. My favourite story is The Bounds of Reason and it features about twenty-five different well-crafted characters who set off on a mission to kill a wounded dragon. I found this narrative exceptional, unpredictable, thrilling with a hell of a twist at the end. This sets Sword of Destiny up brilliantly. <br /><br />I won't go into the details of the stories too much as it might approach spoiler territory. I will confirm that these tales feature many fantasy races as well as mermaids and underwater warriors, showdowns with sorcerers, a group trying to trace a doppleganger, and also meeting Ciri. It features monster hunting of course but not as much and as frequent as The Last Wish. Each The Last Wish story played like a level on the Witcher games. These are less standalone and cleverly building up for the full narrative which will start with Blood of Elves. <br /><br />I adored The Bounds of Reason, A Little Sacrifice and Sword of Destiny. Eternal Flame and A Share of Ice were very average. The final story Something More I really struggled with initially. It follows two timelines as Geralt in a fevered state and I sometimes got confused where and when we were. If it was a full-length story I wouldn't have finished it but I did and I'm glad I fought through as the ending is highly satisfying with setting up what can possible happen in the next outings. <br /><br />I decided to read all of the Witcher books before the TV series is released and I am glad that I have taken on this venture. I've read the first two books within four days and I can't wait to move on further. I often struggle with short stories but I can recommend these highly. The Bound of Reason is one of the top two finest short stories I've ever read alongside Sebastian De Castell - The Fox and the Bowman.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1992116534571097847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3141174875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3141174875" />
    <a title=" Teodora " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"><img alt=" Teodora " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582144281p2/69603149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3141174875?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3141174875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16499716236219819570"><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/02/22/tales-of-the-witcher-the-last-wish-the-witcher-0-5-sword-of-destiny-the-witcher-0-75-by-andrzej-sapkowski/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br/><br/>In the Sword of Destiny, there is no The Voice of Reason chapters, but the action seems to flow somehow even without them because in this short stories book, there is no, let’s say, “time travelling” between the stories. They happen, thank God, at almost the same time, in a continuous present. Except for the last story that got me a bit confused (I don't really do good with stories that leap from one time to the other without telling me EXACTLY what t</span>
  <span id="freeText16499716236219819570" style="display:none"><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/02/22/tales-of-the-witcher-the-last-wish-the-witcher-0-5-sword-of-destiny-the-witcher-0-75-by-andrzej-sapkowski/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br><br>In the Sword of Destiny, there is no The Voice of Reason chapters, but the action seems to flow somehow even without them because in this short stories book, there is no, let’s say, “time travelling” between the stories. They happen, thank God, at almost the same time, in a continuous present. Except for the last story that got me a bit confused (I don't really do good with stories that leap from one time to the other without telling me EXACTLY what the bloody hell they're about to do).<br><br>There are also six stories here:<br><br><b>1. The Bounds of Reason (3.5/5 ⭐)<br>2. A Shard of Ice (5/5 ⭐)<br>3. Eternal Flame (4/5 ⭐)<br>4. A Little Sacrifice (4/5 ⭐)<br>5. The Sword of Destiny (5/5 ⭐)<br>6. Something More (5/5 ⭐)<br>____<br>Total rating for Sword of Destiny: 4.41/5 ⭐</b><br><br><i>
  <b>“Destiny has many faces. Mine is beautiful on the outside and hideous on the inside.”</b>
</i><br><br>Here, the chapters are longer, it seems, and also there is a certain political touch to it, even almost invisible. I tended to get a bit lost sometimes, but got right back when it came to a good old action scene *winks*.<br><br>I especially enjoyed <i>
  <b>A Shard of Ice</b>
</i>. The story is based on H.C. Andersen’s tale <i>
  <b>The Snow Queen</b>
</i>, which is one of my favourite fairy tales ever. So, of course, I enjoyed Mr Sapkowski’s reinterpretation of it. The same goes for that tiny part in The Sword of Destiny where Frexinet’s story is inspired by <i>
  <b>The Wild Swans</b>
</i> fairy tale. Dziękuję bardzo, panie Sapkowski, I really needed that. Also, there was a <i>
  <b>Little Mermaid</b>
</i> reinterpretation in <i>
  <b>A Little Sacrifice</b>
</i> that I enjoyed too. This book was hardcore Andersen-inspired, apparently.<br><br>Apart from that, I realised that I’m not Yennefer’s biggest fan, it tends to repel me somehow, but I don’t entirely dislike her. She’s just tough to love I guess. <br><br>We also get to meet Ciri in this book and hey, that’s what I was waiting for. I also must say that her reunion with Geralt is waaay more different from the one in the TV show and it is ten times better, I'd say.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1582390192i/29006012.png" width="231" height="393" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/cdd5b17d-ccce-45c3-a0fb-107b9ccf4390_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-styled</a>)</span>

<div id="review_1878979060" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1878979060" />
    <a title="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans"><img alt="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587115780p2/7298986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1878979060?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans">✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)</a>
      </span>

        rated it

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25454056-sword-of-destiny">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=set-sail-for-disappointment">set-sail-for-disappointment</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1878979060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15885634943476851118"><b>Uh-oh</b>, I think my boyfriend Geralt is <b>on strike</b>. I mean, why else would the <b>Most Deliciously Scrumptious Witcher Ever aka the Super Hot if Slightly Mutant Monster Slayer</b> (MDSWEakatSHiSMMS™) butcher such a ridiculously low amount of supernatural beasts in this volume? Well, I guess it is also possible that his <s>evil</s> <b>boring twin</b> took over while I was, um, otherwise engaged with some of my other harem, um, boarders and stuff. Or maybe he was <b>abducted by aliens</b>, submitted to vigorous brain reprogramm</span>
  <span id="freeText15885634943476851118" style="display:none"><b>Uh-oh</b>, I think my boyfriend Geralt is <b>on strike</b>. I mean, why else would the <b>Most Deliciously Scrumptious Witcher Ever aka the Super Hot if Slightly Mutant Monster Slayer</b> (MDSWEakatSHiSMMS™) butcher such a ridiculously low amount of supernatural beasts in this volume? Well, I guess it is also possible that his <s>evil</s> <b>boring twin</b> took over while I was, um, otherwise engaged with some of my other harem, um, boarders and stuff. Or maybe he was <b>abducted by aliens</b>, submitted to vigorous brain reprogramming sessions, and then shipped back to us via <b>Expedited Shrimp Express</b> (ESE™)? Who the fish knows? In any case, there is way too little <b>delicious slaughter</b> here and way too much <b>pondering on the meaning of life</b>, destiny, blah blah blah and all that crap. Not to mention the inordinate amount of <b>Suicide-Inducing Lovey Dovey Crap</b> (SILDC™) one has to bravely endure while reading this book. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517073250ra/24946837.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Indeed.</i><br><br><b>Okay</b>, so there's some <b>really good</b>, err, what's the word for this? Oh, yes, I remember now, "stuff" is the <b>technical term</b> I'm looking for. So yes, there is definitely some <b>good stuff</b> here: a little bit of <b>intrigue</b>, a pinch of <b>adventure</b>, a dash of <b>Let's Gleefully Hack at Things</b> (LGHaT™), a speck of <b>humor</b>, a drop of <b>shenanigans</b> and a soupçon of my <b>homicidally sexy boyfriend</b>. Alas, unfortunately and stuff, sufficient to make this short story collection <b>as yummilicious as The Last Wish</b> this wasn't. Most of the stories begin <b>stupendously enough</b>, I'll give you that, my Little Barnacles. One opens with a <b>basilisk</b>, <b>
  <i>free warrior women</i>
</b> and <b>crayfish</b>. Which got me all excite because coming across my freshwater cousins in books always <b>makes my exoskeleton tingle</b> and stuff. Another story begins with <b>tentacles</b>, <b>serrated claws</b> and <b>mountains of exploding trash</b>. Which brought back fond memories of my past life as <b>Marjory the Trash Heap</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517082217i/24947854.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>Ah, good times.</i><br><br><b>Then</b> there is the story that kicks off with a delightfully <b>capricious mermaid</b> and later introduces super, um, friendly <b>sea creatures</b>. And then the story that starts with most, um, welcoming <b>monsters</b>. And <b>severed limbs</b>. Oh, and let's not forget the one with the <b>dryads</b>! So, you see, all the stories in this collection begin <b>quite gloriously indeed</b>. The problem is, most of them then proceed to deflate like the <b>proverbial (if bloody shrimping) soufflé</b>. Because too many pointless <b>ramblings</b> and endless dialogues, not enough <b>blood-shedding</b>. Because too much <b>allergy-inducing relationship drama</b>, not enough action. And don't get me started on <b>Yennefer</b>. Actually, no, please DO get me started on her. To think I <s>locked her up in my harem</s> kindly <b>offered her asylum</b> after reading The Last Wish! She was cool! She was <b>cunning</b>! She was badass! She was <b>ho</b>t! She was mine! But now? It's pretty obvious the aliens <b>kidnapped and then brainwashed her</b> like they did Geralt. Why else would she act like such an <b>exasperatingly selfish</b>—or is it selfishly exasperating? I forget—<b>bitch</b>? And the angst! Bloody stinking fish, the <b>angst</b>! There's enough of it here to feed a battalion of <b>Thoroughly Frustrated New Adult Fangirls</b> (TFNAF™)! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517080063ra/24947668.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Yeah, more or less.</i><br><br><b>But hey, it's not ALL bad</b>. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>Just so you know, I deny ever writing what you are about to read. It only exists in your alcohol-drenched little head. You shouldn't drink and read, you know. It's not the most sensible behavior, you know. Follow my example! Drink chamomile tea at all times!<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517078749i/24947347.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That detector of yours is obviously broken, Young Man of the Silly Costume. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I mean, there's a <b>super cute kid</b> in two of the stories. Her name is Ciri. She made my black, withered heart do <b>all kind of weird things</b>. First of all, it started beating, which was kind of, you know, <b>spooky and stuff</b>. Then it kinda sorta felt like it was getting <b>slightly squished</b> and stuff. Strange, err, what was that technical term again? Oh yes, stuff. Strange stuff. Indeed. <b>Disgusting, too</b>. You have to admit that feeling so <b>revoltingly emotional and human</b> isn't really in my line of work. I find the idea both terribly repulsive and horribly inadequate, to be honest. <b>So I very logically kidnapped Ciri</b>. For her own good, obviously. Also, she'll make great <b>blackmail material</b>. I won't release her until my Geralt returns to his former MDSWEakatSHiSMMS™ self. <b>Muahahahaha and stuff</b>.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>This is the end of the paragraph you thought you read but didn't because you're drunk and because I never wrote it. You're welcome.</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br> <br>➽ And the moral of this <b>The Evil Russians™ Quite Evidently Replaced my Geralt with a Sappy Doppelgänger That's It I'm Unleashing the Shrimps on the Kremlin and Getting the Real Him Back to the Harem and Stuff Crappy Non Review</b> (TERQERmGwaSDTIIUtSonKaGtRHBttHaSCNR™) is: my pet Algernon <b>misses his monster friends</b>, Mr Sapkowski. Please bring them back, even if it's just to have them <b>slightly slaughtered</b> by my Geralt. Algernon feels <b>awfully lost</b> without them, you see. I mean, look at the <b>poor thing</b>! Doesn't he look utterly helpless and <b>completely befuddled</b> to you? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517080582ra/24947711.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>So please do the charitable thing, Mr Sapkowski</b>. Bring my mutant beast slayer back and <b>Make Algernon Gleeful Again</b> (MAGA™)! <br><br>· <b>Book 1</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1815326876" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a> ★★★★★<br>· <b>Book 3</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1878979579" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood of Elves</a> ★★★<br>· <b>Book 4</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1878980031" rel="nofollow noopener">The Time of Contempt</a> ★★<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[<b>Pre-review nonsense</b>]<br><br><b>Geralt</b>, dear boy, we need to talk. I locked you up in my High Security Harem because you were a <b>super hot monster slayer</b>, not for your disgusting <b>love sick puppy tendencies</b>. So you stop this revolting display of <b>vile maudlin sentimentality</b> right this minute, or I'm sending you to the <b>DNF Graveyard</b> until you become yourself again, <b>you hear me</b>?!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1516991160ra/24939315.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>What? You didn't know Geralt looked like a toast with tiny arms? You really are clueless, aren't you, my Little Barnacles?</i><br><br>➽ Full <b>Who The Bloody Fish Are You and What Have You Done with My Sexey Badass Mutant Boyfriend Crappy Non Review</b> (WTBFAYaWHYDwMSBMBCNR™) to come.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1765409250?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25454056-sword-of-destiny">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1765409250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15017129701325323015">This is a second collection of short stories featuring Geralt of Rivia. If I understand correctly it was written before The Last Wish, but chronologically comes after that one. The stories of this anthology are longer and less funny although one of them can be considered to be entirely humorous. <br/> <br/>As most of the people already know Geralt is a witcher. This means he hunts monsters for living. He is also considered to be a mutant by many as his training included undergoing some chemical (herbs) an</span>
  <span id="freeText15017129701325323015" style="display:none">This is a second collection of short stories featuring Geralt of Rivia. If I understand correctly it was written before The Last Wish, but chronologically comes after that one. The stories of this anthology are longer and less funny although one of them can be considered to be entirely humorous. <br> <br>As most of the people already know Geralt is a witcher. This means he hunts monsters for living. He is also considered to be a mutant by many as his training included undergoing some chemical (herbs) and magical treatment that left him not-quite-human. So what does the guy do in this anthology? He is being lovesick - he is madly in love with Yennefer, he does his damned to escape what he thinks is his destiny, he follows his Codex which does not allow him to kill intelligent monsters. Have you notice something is missing in this description? <br> <br>Exactly, the monster hunter does everything, but <i>hunting monsters</i>. This makes even one of the characters wonder how the heck he made his living with his nonexistent work-related income; it feels kind of like this:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475520172i/20729802._SX540_.jpg" width="460" height="358" alt="Lazy" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Unsurprisingly Geralt is broke most of the time. <br> <br>I would like to talk about the love part of the book. What is a cornerstone cliché of a romance novel? The one without which the whole genre would not exists at all? It is a standard situation when two people are deeply in love with each other, but both of them keep creating obstacles that prevent them from being together, knowing exactly what they are doing. I mean imagine two people meet each other, fall in love, get married right away within a couple of pages, and fall into a standard married routine. Who in the right mind would read such a boring book? <br> <br>Geralt and Yennefer is exactly such couple. The troubles they go to NOT be with each other boggle the mind. As you might guess these situations feel a little old. They felt old during Shakespeare time actually. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475520172i/20729803._SX540_.jpg" width="460" height="302" alt="Romeo and Juliette" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>At least in the Great Bard's tale it were families that kept the kids separated. <br> <br>It was not a bad anthology despite my criticism, but it did resulted in a lower rating by half a star. I am also willing to cut some slack due to a fact that it was the first written installment of the series. The next book promptly goes to my to-read shelf. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15017129701325323015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1958644466" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1958644466" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487160141p2/8836060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1958644466?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25454056-sword-of-destiny">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8836060-michelle?shelf=witcherverse">witcherverse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1958644466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1906756926261345049">(Review of 2 books: “The Last Wish” and “The Sword of Destiny)<br/><br/>It’s been a while since I’ve indulged in some sword and sorcery, and I’m happy to have come upon a trailer of “The Witcher 3: Wild Hunt” on Youtube. It’s visually stunning and highly fascinating! I wanted to learn more about the game and, to cut this story short (I guess you know where this is going anyway), discovered Andrzej Sapkowski’s written wonders. I’m sure the games are awesome, but I’m quite glad that I can immerse myself in </span>
  <span id="freeText1906756926261345049" style="display:none">(Review of 2 books: “The Last Wish” and “The Sword of Destiny)<br /><br />It’s been a while since I’ve indulged in some sword and sorcery, and I’m happy to have come upon a trailer of “The Witcher 3: Wild Hunt” on Youtube. It’s visually stunning and highly fascinating! I wanted to learn more about the game and, to cut this story short (I guess you know where this is going anyway), discovered Andrzej Sapkowski’s written wonders. I’m sure the games are awesome, but I’m quite glad that I can immerse myself in "The Witcher" universe through my preferred medium.<br /><br />“The Last Wish” and “The Sword of Destiny” are each a collection of short, inter-connected stories that read very much like a character study. A study of the witcher, Geralt of Rivia, and his tormented relationship with the concept of destiny. The stories are nonlinear, but the links are easy to follow, and not every story turns out the way you might think or expect.<br /><br />It's really hard for me to convey the depth of these collection of stories. They have a range of tone -- humor, romance, adventure, intrigue -- that is amazing. The writing is contemporary and yet has a resonance that feels timeless. It reminds me of Tolkien, in that there is a depth to the world Sapkowski has created that makes you feel like it's been around for a very long time. The books rank right up there amidst the fantasy genre as most immersive and entertaining. Sapkowski has an interesting way of setting up a story according to traditional fantasy and fairy tale fashion, then allowing the darkest facets of our own world bleed through the pages. Complicated questions about morality, religion, diversity, progress, and love are incorporated into the stories and the characters.<br /><br />I fell in love with Geralt and his story,and he never disappoints with his perspective or his choices. He is relatable in a way that he is not the hyper self-righteous paragon of justice like many fantasy protagonists. He's merely a tradesman, of an albeit interesting line of work, trying somewhat desperately to keep his head above water and do the right thing. There's something of us all in Geralt in that respect.<br /><br />I find the stories well written, suspenseful and engaging. The characters are diverse, colorful and relatable. One of the treasures of Sapkowski's style is how much of the plot is revealed through character interactions. Conversations flow naturally yet give all the necessary exposition and world building. The characters are interesting, believable and three dimensional no matter how small their role. The stories are at times bleak and grim, and yet there is an odd sense of whimsy like you might find in a classic Grimm's fairy tale. They can be comical or tragic but never contrived.<br /><br />Overall, these are highly satisfying reads and I would highly recommend this to anyone who has a penchant for tough and gritty heroes who slay monsters and protect even the dumbest jerks from themselves with wisdom, dry wit, swordplay and a grounded sense of realism. Now I'm doubly excited to move on to the main series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1906756926261345049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Sapkowski, you f-ing rule.<br /><br />It doesn't seem like the Swedish publishers will publish any more Sapkowskibooks, and all I can say is; Your Loss, man.<br /><br />Luckily, the Witcher Saga is available in English!<br /><br />Everything about this book is awesome, from the characters to the world, to the humor and the fighting scenes. (unless you are a ghoul or something, and then Geralt will find you and destroy you.)<br /><br />So, if you haven't yet read any Andrzej Sapkowski, do it now. Yesterday if you could.   <b>4 STARS, destined for great things ★★★★✩</b>
</u><br/><i>
  <blockquote>
<b>This book is for you if… </b>high fantasy with room for humour and modernised language suits your tastes. Be prepared for a lot of angsty romance and badass fighting scenes.</blockquote>
</i><br/><b>⤐ <i>Preface.</i></b><br/>Can we please, collectively, complain to Netflix for taking off <i>The Witcher</i> soundtrack of Spotify? I literally need to listen to <i>Toss a coin to your witcher</i> until I shout it from my grave.<br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1578482886ra/28736120.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>UPDATE</b>: It seems our collective karening has helped. I've not only enjoyed the orig</span>
  <span id="freeText17774952826200686708" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>4 STARS, destined for great things ★★★★✩</b>
</u><br><i>
  <blockquote>
<b>This book is for you if… </b>high fantasy with room for humour and modernised language suits your tastes. Be prepared for a lot of angsty romance and badass fighting scenes.</blockquote>
</i><br><b>⤐ <i>Preface.</i></b><br>Can we please, collectively, complain to Netflix for taking off <i>The Witcher</i> soundtrack of Spotify? I literally need to listen to <i>Toss a coin to your witcher</i> until I shout it from my grave.<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1578482886ra/28736120.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>UPDATE</b>: It seems our collective karening has helped. I've not only enjoyed the original, but also this amazing <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HiXY-xghv-Q" rel="nofollow noopener">cover</a> by the incredibly talented <a href="https://www.youtube.com/user/VioletaOrlandi" rel="nofollow noopener">Orletta Vicover</a><br><br><b>⤐ <i>Overall.</i></b><br>Different from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3094975027?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a> in its style of adventures but still very enjoyable, this collection of short stories is less a sequence of cases, as was the previous book, but more of a deep dive into what shape and traits Geralt's character has, which is very useful considering I've not read the following books or played the game.<br><br><b>A close up on the witcher characters</b> is the unofficial title of <i>Sword of Destiny</i> book, I swear! It was very enjoyable to remeet with the men and women I came to love in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3094975027?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a>. They are now a bit less of a mystery and more like old friends to me.<br><br><b>World(-building).</b> It was more of a world deepening in my experience. The political dynamics became a bit clearer, as did the ethnic diversity which leads to an overall improved understanding of the world.<br><br><b>The arch of suspense.</b> Hmm [in Henry Cavill's voice].<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1579357492ra/28799873.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Some of the stories were really exciting and others kinda had me skimming the pages for dialogue. This is probably my biggest point of critique. Still a page-turner overall.<br><br>You will find me in bed, inhaling the entire Witcher Season. Oh, and harassing both Netflix and Spotify on Twitter, for obvious reasons.<br><br><b>⤐ <i>What’s happening.</i></b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‘Doubts. Only evil, sir, never has any. But no one can escape his destiny.’</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Whether he knows it or not, Geralt of Rivia is getting closer to his fate with every step he takes in this unusual but enlightening collection of short stories. Dragons, mermaids, dopplers and dryads, this book challenges him in very untypical ways.<br><blockquote>
<b>Con:</b><br>⇢ <i>the monsters are getting bigger</i><br>⇢ <i>destiny has fangs, not feathers</i><br>⇢ <i>incompetent morons everywhere</i><br><b>Pro:</b><br>⇢ <i>more dandelion</i><br>⇢ <i>more yennefer</i><br>⇢ <i>more angsty romance</i>
</blockquote><br>_____________________<br><b>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=audio">audio</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1997300743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15452420833576606326">The Bounds of Reason - ⭐️⭐️⭐️ DRAGONS and a shocking twist<br/>A Shard of Ice - ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ Yennefer and Geralt angst (with hints of a certain infamous stuffed unicorn 🦄 )<br/>Eternal Flame - ⭐️⭐️⭐️ An intro to Dudu and Dopplers.<br/>A Little Sacrifice - ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ Mermaids, love and sea monsters<br/>The Sword of Destiny - ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ A lost princess, Dryads and the bonds of destiny <br/>Something More - ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ The fall of a kingdom, and a law of surprise<br/><br/>I really enjoyed this short story collection, more so than the first <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40603587.The_Last_Wish__The_Witcher___0_5_' title='The Last Wish (The Witcher, #0.5) by Andrzej Sapkowski' rel='nofollow noopener'>The</a></span>
  <span id="freeText15452420833576606326" style="display:none">The Bounds of Reason - ⭐️⭐️⭐️ DRAGONS and a shocking twist<br />A Shard of Ice - ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ Yennefer and Geralt angst (with hints of a certain infamous stuffed unicorn 🦄 )<br />Eternal Flame - ⭐️⭐️⭐️ An intro to Dudu and Dopplers.<br />A Little Sacrifice - ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ Mermaids, love and sea monsters<br />The Sword of Destiny - ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ A lost princess, Dryads and the bonds of destiny <br />Something More - ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ The fall of a kingdom, and a law of surprise<br /><br />I really enjoyed this short story collection, more so than the first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40603587.The_Last_Wish__The_Witcher___0_5_" title="The Last Wish (The Witcher, #0.5) by Andrzej Sapkowski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a>. I think it helped that I had a better grounding in the lore and history of the world, and was less put off by the odd time jumps and pacing. I will say that the second half is a lot snappier in pace, and introduces the wonderful Ciri, which helped propel this to a 4 star read for me.<br /><br />As always, I love Yennefer and Geralt. I love the complexity to their relationship, often with years in between their meetings, yet the undeniable love they share for each other. Destiny and more bind them together, and their exchanges are always a delight to read. <br /><br />I’m really excited to dive into the ‘proper’ novels in 2020 now that I feel I have a good background knowledge to our heroes. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1973162806072923268">This second short story collection is unfortunately the weakest part of the Witcher universe that I have read. It is not on the level of <i>The Last Wish</i>, the stories feel mashed together without the same sense of purpose as in the other book, and they are less exciting, less symbolic and less epic.<br/><br/>However, I love experiencing the world of the Witcher and following Geralt of Rivia and Yennefer of Vengerberg on their adventures (even though Yennefer is dreadfully annoying in this book compared to ot</span>
  <span id="freeText1973162806072923268" style="display:none">This second short story collection is unfortunately the weakest part of the Witcher universe that I have read. It is not on the level of <i>The Last Wish</i>, the stories feel mashed together without the same sense of purpose as in the other book, and they are less exciting, less symbolic and less epic.<br /><br />However, I love experiencing the world of the Witcher and following Geralt of Rivia and Yennefer of Vengerberg on their adventures (even though Yennefer is dreadfully annoying in this book compared to other volumes). <i>Sword of Destiny</i> is also very much worth reading for a Witcher fan as it provides a proper introduction to Ciri, adding more context to the happenings of <i>The Last Wish</i> and the main saga.<br /><br />Overall, this is a decent book, although it doesn’t quite fulfil its huge potential.<br /><br /><b>Witcher reviews:</b><br />#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/792532185" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a><br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1890591117" rel="nofollow noopener">Sword of Destiny</a><br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793290591" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood of Elves</a></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473211537" href="/book/show/18215192-sword-of-destiny">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86504940-will-j-r-gwynne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86504940-will-j-r-gwynne?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2940744907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11496380145060689190">My expanded review has now been placed on BookNest - <a href='https://booknest.eu/component/k2/william/1876-sword-of-destiny-the-witcher-0-75-by-andrzej-sapkowski-book-review' rel='nofollow noopener'>BookNest - Sword of Destiny</a><br/><br/>So Sword of Destiny is the second book in The Witcher Saga, but dates before The Last Wish. Many of the same characters are encountered as are many new monsters, one being a doppler.<br/><br/>Some stories were great, such as the one that seems to be a bit inspired by the little mermaid. It was surprisingly emotional and showed a completely different side to Geralt of Rivia that I have longed to see.<br/><br/>The story of a mimic who can</span>
  <span id="freeText11496380145060689190" style="display:none">My expanded review has now been placed on BookNest - <a href="https://booknest.eu/component/k2/william/1876-sword-of-destiny-the-witcher-0-75-by-andrzej-sapkowski-book-review" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest - Sword of Destiny</a><br /><br />So Sword of Destiny is the second book in The Witcher Saga, but dates before The Last Wish. Many of the same characters are encountered as are many new monsters, one being a doppler.<br /><br />Some stories were great, such as the one that seems to be a bit inspired by the little mermaid. It was surprisingly emotional and showed a completely different side to Geralt of Rivia that I have longed to see.<br /><br />The story of a mimic who can change into anyone and adopt their mannerisms was hilarious, and rightly caused mayhem! Gerald showed his honourable side once again in this and calmly strode towards the solution. He can be so cool!<br /><br />However, it does confuse me how Geralt is sometimes completely calm and executes plans perfectly, but becomes somewhat of a bumbling man in other stories, particularly around Yennefer. <br /><br />So overall, Sword of Destiny was another fun experience with Geralt of Rivia in this world of monsters and hunters. His camaraderie with Dandelion was a high point once again, as were the interesting creatures that feature. I look forward to reading the other novels in the future.</span>

<div id="review_2387487884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2387487884" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2387487884?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316389709" href="/book/show/25318857-sword-of-destiny">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2387487884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2727393625989501713"><b>3.5/5 stars.<br/><br/>The compelling characterisation of Geralt and the imaginative world of Slavic lore and fairy-tale retellings continue in <i>Sword of Destiny</i>, the second collection of prequel short stories.</b> <br/><br/><i>Sword of Destiny</i> was published after the first three full-length novels of <i>The Witcher</i> series. As a new reader to the series, however, I was able to read the books in chronological order which is quite essential as this instalment served as the bridge between <i>The Last Wish</i> and <i>Blood of Elves</i>. <br/><br/>I found</span>
  <span id="freeText2727393625989501713" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5 stars.<br /><br />The compelling characterisation of Geralt and the imaginative world of Slavic lore and fairy-tale retellings continue in <i>Sword of Destiny</i>, the second collection of prequel short stories.</b> <br /><br /><i>Sword of Destiny</i> was published after the first three full-length novels of <i>The Witcher</i> series. As a new reader to the series, however, I was able to read the books in chronological order which is quite essential as this instalment served as the bridge between <i>The Last Wish</i> and <i>Blood of Elves</i>. <br /><br />I found that <i>The Last Wish</i> is overall a better book than <i>Sword of Destiny</i> with the connectivity of having a frame story wrapped around the short stories. This latter book feels more disjointed for me, and I did not enjoy Geralt's development as much, especially when it comes to his overwhelming obsession with Yennefer, whom I do not like much. It pains me to see how Geralt seemed to lose a bit of himself and his badassery whenever he is around the sorceress. It didn't help that she can be quite a bitch at times. <br /><br />There are also less 'killing monsters' and more romance in this collection of Geralt's adventures. Truth be told, I don't typically favour a lot of romance in my stories. Nonetheless, the tale which borrowed from <i>The Little Mermaid</i> was one of the best in this book, and the love story herein is quite touching. Dandelion, the bard, can aggravate me as much as make me laugh, but the ending of <i>'A Little Sacrifice'</i> brought tears to my eyes.<br /><br />Fascinating creatures continue to pop up, and my favourite in this book was the mimic or the doppler - a creature which not only can mimic one's physiognomy but also one's psychology - from the tale <i>'Eternal Flame'</i>. The story on its own did not seem to contribute much to the overarching story of Geralt except to again solidify the inaccurate general perception of witchers being cold-blooded killers. <br /><br />However, the arc that I was most looking forward to was the titular story, Sword of Destiny. Ever since I've read the short story <i>'A Question of Price'</i> in <i>The Last Wish</i>, I was waiting for this crucial moment; the introduction of Princess Ciri and her first meeting with Geralt. And it was a darn good one, which was made all the more interesting with the appearance of the mysterious dryads and their protected land of Brokilon where all humans cannot trespass on pain of death.<br /><br />The final piece <i>'Something More'</i> was the clincher to this theme of destiny. As much as the White Wolf did not appear to believe in destiny (or perhaps refused to), it will not let him go. And war is coming with the invasion of the Nilfgaardians. <br /><br />All I can say is that if you are a fan of <i>The Witcher</i>, do not pass up on this novel. While I find a few of the stories here less than impressive, the last two are essential to the storyline, and the overall book is still enjoyable.<br /><br /><i>You can purchase the book from <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Sword-Destiny-Witcher-Book-4-ebook/dp/B00W22J07S/" rel="nofollow noopener"><u><b>Amazon</b></u></a> | <a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/Sword-Destiny-Andrzej-Sapkowski/9780316389709/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener"><u><b>Book Depository (Free shipping worldwide)</b></u></a></i><br /><br /><i>You can also find <a href="http://novelnotions.net/2019/07/24/sword-of-destiny-the-witcher-2/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a>, and my other reviews at <a href="http://novelnotions.net/category/book-reviews/tss-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions.</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2727393625989501713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3111117022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3111117022" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3111117022?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25454056-sword-of-destiny">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2020-shelf">2020-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3111117022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5542239790841687933">Okay, so I've arrived very late to the Witcher party. I feel like I really ought to be embarrassed or something, too, but I've decided just to roll with it. <br/><br/>I... might have become a fanboy.<br/><br/>I mean, shoot, I've got Cavill in my head as the penultimate Geralt. Yennifer is someone I think I'll always love. I've got that whole season stuck in my head, and reading these two collections preceding the first official novel has made something very clear to me.<br/><br/>The first season IS these to books. <br/><br/>Maybe not </span>
  <span id="freeText5542239790841687933" style="display:none">Okay, so I've arrived very late to the Witcher party. I feel like I really ought to be embarrassed or something, too, but I've decided just to roll with it. <br /><br />I... might have become a fanboy.<br /><br />I mean, shoot, I've got Cavill in my head as the penultimate Geralt. Yennifer is someone I think I'll always love. I've got that whole season stuck in my head, and reading these two collections preceding the first official novel has made something very clear to me.<br /><br />The first season IS these to books. <br /><br />Maybe not a few of the stories, or nowhere near this form, and a couple really deepen the connection between Geralt and Yennifer, and the whole cycle in the tv show that gives us a close look at Yennifer but it doesn't show in these two books... but ASIDE from that, I loved meeting the dragon, getting the Destiny setup from new angles, and, let's face it... I LOVED the story about the mermaid and hope to hell we get that in the next season. :)<br /><br />Did I mention that I'm fanboying?<br /><br />I'm having so much fun with these. Now let me be clear about one thing. The fantasy element is well done but not wholly original. The characters are rife with riffs in mythology in general and the interactions are easily familiar and fun for anyone who enjoys fantasy in general. <br /><br />What makes this special is the sheer force of personality, of characterization, of the FEELS. And let's not forget the fun. I'm having SO much fun. :)<br /><br />I guess it's not that much of a surprise that the series is still growing in popularity. I barely even knew about the books until after the games started taking off, and I still haven't played the games yet. For shame, right?<br /><br />I'm still happy. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5542239790841687933" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2266860707" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2266860707" />
    <a title="Prongs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43102815-prongs"><img alt="Prongs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433280720p2/43102815.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2266860707?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Prongs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Prongs" href="/user/show/43102815-prongs">Prongs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473211537" href="/book/show/18215192-sword-of-destiny">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2266860707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8908685270414906243">Humans and Elves and Dwarves and Trolls. Oh, and Women.<br/><br/>That's what parts of this book felt like. Like women are a different, lesser race. I think the way women are depicted in this book is problematic. To have a medieval world behaving in a medieval way about women is something, to have clever and heroic protagonists going along with it is something else entirely. I really don't have anything against a hero who has lots of sex with lots of women. As a guy, I get why this is appealing to a Fantas</span>
  <span id="freeText8908685270414906243" style="display:none">Humans and Elves and Dwarves and Trolls. Oh, and Women.<br /><br />That's what parts of this book felt like. Like women are a different, lesser race. I think the way women are depicted in this book is problematic. To have a medieval world behaving in a medieval way about women is something, to have clever and heroic protagonists going along with it is something else entirely. I really don't have anything against a hero who has lots of sex with lots of women. As a guy, I get why this is appealing to a Fantasy author. But I need strong characters. I need some non-sexualized girls. This had too many bits about women being annoying in the background for me to feel confortable reading it. Too many bits about women speaking their mind and somehow coming out less likable for it. So much effort in that direction that it feels like the author himself thinks that women are second-rate people, only tolerable inside a bedroom or a kitchen. With race equality as a recurring theme throughout the book, this is really clumsy.<br /><br />And this was published in the 90's. It's always disappointing when this mentality shows up in an old fantasy book, but at least it's kind of predictable. It's like finding racism in a 19th century travel-adventure novel. But today... This should not be left unnoticed.<br /><br />Am I supposed to like Dandelion at this point ? Apparently, the author thinks being a dick is a lovable trait because he keeps coming up and I can't believe this guy was meant as a long lasting character. This is not a good Rogue, this is a living embodiment of everything I hate about Fantasy.<br /><br />And I am supposed to like Yennefer at all ? After research, I've read how Sapkowski brags about her not being a fantasy stereotype, which only confirms that he is only capable of writing either stupid-giggling-just-for-fantasy-sex-girls or cold condescending bitches (still up for sex mind you). Yennefer is the least likable female character I have ever found in Fantasy, and it is not because of unintentional sexism from my part. I don't understand in what world this character was meant as lovable. I genuinely thought that all the textual evidence was meant to foreshadow tragedy and how Geralt could only suffer with someone like this. It is now obvious that it was meant to be also part of the novels, and now I have too much info to really care about her or their relationship.<br /><br />Now about the storytelling itself, I have mixed feelings.<br />I don't know about Polish, I read the English translation because the French one is crap (real real crap) and with now 3 different translations tested, I am pretty confident that the source material is far from great literature. The best I could get from this book was the Audible version. Peter Kenny did an amazing job with it, but even with David French's translation (which is the best I encountered so far), some bits were truly painful. It had some good chapters in the beginning, but this flirting with long-term plot got boring real fast. The long thoughts and dialogs during The Brokilon part were particularly clumsy, and The Beltane chapter with Yennefer might be one of the worst things I have ever read inside a success Fantasy novel, so bad you would think Terry Goodkind wrote it.<br /><br />Worst thing is, I really really loved Ciri, and I think she is everything this series needed. We'll see about that. It's a shame her chapters were so weak.<br /><br />I rated The Last Wish 3 stars because there's only so much plot you can expect from a short stories book, but now it is getting closer and closer to a novel, I really have doubts about Sapkowski's ability to keep these characters interesting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8908685270414906243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16598455200934463418">This is the second prequel short story collection that begins The Witcher series.<br/><br/>Like the former anthology, this follows Witcher, Geralt. Unlike the former anthology it largely deviates from detailing his work and the many beasts, creatures, and magical beings that roam these lands, and instead focuses on more personal topics, including his relationships with women and his preoccupation with one female in particular.<br/><br/>I found I appreciated the contents of this one less as it did not contain the sc</span>
  <span id="freeText16598455200934463418" style="display:none">This is the second prequel short story collection that begins The Witcher series.<br /><br />Like the former anthology, this follows Witcher, Geralt. Unlike the former anthology it largely deviates from detailing his work and the many beasts, creatures, and magical beings that roam these lands, and instead focuses on more personal topics, including his relationships with women and his preoccupation with one female in particular.<br /><br />I found I appreciated the contents of this one less as it did not contain the scenes of magic and bloodshed that I was anticipating but it was interesting to get to know this elusive witcher a little better. I also loved how, just like in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40603587.The_Last_Wish__The_Witcher___0_5_" title="The Last Wish (The Witcher, #0.5) by Andrzej Sapkowski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a>, the stories were interconnected to make a chronological history of Geralt's life. I think I'm ready to move onto the full works in this series, now though.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2924817391" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2924817391" />
    <a title="Edward" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13459162-edward"><img alt="Edward" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579803798p2/13459162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2924817391?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward" href="/user/show/13459162-edward">Edward</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316389" href="/book/show/42054761-sword-of-destiny-tales-of-the-witcher">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13459162-edward?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13459162-edward?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2924817391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9695560977789229727"><b>Check out my review for Sword of Destiny by Andrzej Sapkowski on Grimdark Magazine here: <a href='https://www.grimdarkmagazine.com/review-sword-of-destiny-by-andrzej-sapkowski/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Grimdark Magazine</a></b><br/><br/>Sword of Destiny is a slavic fantasy book that contains the brilliance captured by the video game series, as well as the repertoire of characters that Andrej Sapkowski has at his disposal. This second collection of short stories in the world of the Witcher is a book that those who enjoyed the first collection, will love, as it brings more of the same.<br/><br/><b>’What a hideous smile I have, Geralt thou</b></span>
  <span id="freeText9695560977789229727" style="display:none"><b>Check out my review for Sword of Destiny by Andrzej Sapkowski on Grimdark Magazine here: <a href="https://www.grimdarkmagazine.com/review-sword-of-destiny-by-andrzej-sapkowski/" rel="nofollow noopener">Grimdark Magazine</a></b><br /><br />Sword of Destiny is a slavic fantasy book that contains the brilliance captured by the video game series, as well as the repertoire of characters that Andrej Sapkowski has at his disposal. This second collection of short stories in the world of the Witcher is a book that those who enjoyed the first collection, will love, as it brings more of the same.<br /><br /><b>’What a hideous smile I have, Geralt thought, reaching for his sword. What a hideous face I have, and how hideously I squint. So, is that what I look like? Damn’</b><br /><br />Geralt is such a great character, we have now had two whole books to get to know him as a Witcher, and understand his motives and background. Sword of Destiny does a good job of building upon the foundations of his character, lain by The Last Wish. Although still a short story collection, the development of Geralt is satisfying and evident much more in this volume. These chapters are linked, through characters that appear in multiple short stories, and Geralt’s engagement with them creates a fun experience. <br /><br />Geralt’s cool-rating went up and up with each conversation, his witty and intelligent self shining in this collection. However, what frustrated me was his bumbling and pretty strange character when in the company of Yennefer, though maybe I’m still too used to the Geralt from the Witcher 3.<br /><br /><b>‘Don’t teach me how to trade you prat’</b><br /><br />The stories in Sword of Destiny contained some fantastic examples of fantasy done at it’s highest, with dragons, dwarves, shape-shifters and doppelgängers, ferocious monsters and high-magic. The variety ensures that you will love at least one of the stories and enjoy most of them. I loved how different each story was, with their own morals and messages they portrayed. This is one of Sapkowski’s many strengths, where he carves a small book into a unique experience that challenges your ideas. The realisation that this is a fantasy book is pushed to the back of your mind, where it can also be perceived as a social commentary regarding issues that are still relevant today.<br /><br />Also there’s swords. Lots of different swords. It’s pretty awesome, and the action is well-done, however rare. The dialogue was a big step-up in this second chapter, and the exchanges between characters was enjoyable and fun. Dandelion comes into his own in this, showing the many layers of his character (more layers than Shrek!). I also enjoyed the introduction of Ciri, a character so central to the Witcher 3. Although it was equally amusing and shocking to listen to the narrater’s thick Scottish portrayal of her.<br /><br /><b>’Has anyone ever told you that you are gorgeous?’</b><br /><br /><b>4/5 - A similar but satisfying continuation of the Witcher series. A step-up from The Last Wish that delivers emotionally and physically punching stories. The variety keeps you on your toes, and the development is good. Geralt is still a very cool guy, and I look forward to beginning the full novels of these soon. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9695560977789229727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
